It was a lot to take in at first! But having read reviews before I bought, I knew I would need baby powder and baby oil (don't waste your money on wax-off! Baby oil gets wax off of anything.) So I already had some. I have sensitive skin so I got the ones with aloe and vitamin e from J&J.<br />The wax took a while to heat up, but its February in Vermont so I'm sure it was frozen when I got it. Had a mild plastic smell for a moment, but went away quickly. This wax is supposed to be for sensitive skin so I was hopeful that the comments about the mess and not pulling the hair out would be based on operator error. It is, mostly. The hair has to be a little longer than normal for this to work well. The hair on my chin wasn't quite long enough for it, but it did my eyebrows beautifully, after I figured out that cooling time is really important for this wax. MAKE SURE you let the wax cool long enough, and don't get impatient like I did, before you pull the strip. As far as mess goes, its wax. Its supposed to stick to everything it touches. Put some newspaper down to cover your work surfaces, use the drip collars, and just roll it all up and throw it away when you're done. Sticky crap all over everything is a non-issue this way.<br />Overall, very happy with it. I give it four stars only because there are things you don't need included, and things you really need left out of this kit. Powder and wax remover instead of concealer and lotion maybe?

  142. I am very surprised by the number of complaints about this product and I also noticed that the biggest gripe is the creme wax that comes in the starter kit. That is why it's called a starter kit, it doesn't include EVERYTHING. Please read up on which product is best suited for your skin and hair type. Creme wax is made for sensitive skin and baby fine hair. Also, for those who complain that it didn't remove any hair, apply wax in the direction of your hair growth, press the cloth strip over the wax and smooth firmly in the direction of your hair growth. Lastly, remove strip quickly opposite direction of hair growth. Do not let wax cool before removing strip, remove while still warm. One more thing.. NEVER reapply wax to already waxed skin as it will cause burns. The wax not only removes hair but exfoliates as well, leaving you with sensitive new skin.<br /><br />Please read all instructions before using to prevent disasters.

This does an incredible amount to prevent in grown hairs. I can definitely attest to this since I'm lazy and wanted to see if it made a difference. There is a substantial difference in the irritation and painful in grown hairs that occur without moisturizing and the smooth sailing that accompanies exfoliating and moisturizing. We're fans of [[ASIN:B002Y26RVI Banana Boat Aloe Vera Sun Burn Relief Gel, 8-Ounce Bottles (Pack of 4)]] , but I'm sure there are other products that would work just great too.<br /><br />Another tip is that it's okay to apply the wax sparingly / thin. It still works great. I used very little and didn't miss or break a single hair (at least that we could see).<br /><br />The first few times we ever got waxed we'd take painkillers (ibuprofen worked best for us) 1/2 an hour before to reduce the pain and swelling, but we're quite used to the feeling now so don't bother.<br /><br />In the end this turned into a great success and we will be saving a ton of money. I'll still visit the spa to visit our teacher and since I'm not sure if I want to trust my eyebrows to a first timer, but the bills for waxing will be much lower.<br /><br />I'll repeat a tip that I've read several times because I think it's important. Ask lots of questions about how to do it or why the professional is doing things the way s/he does. It will give you the best chance of success at home.

  386. I really wanted to give my opinion about this waxing unit because it's gotten some harsh reviews. First of all, WAX IS STICKY!<br />I think anyone who has not waxed before, should try a professional first to get an idea of how to use it.<br />Melted wax is extremely sticky, which is why it takes your hair off<br />MAKE SURE TO HAVE BABY OIL ON HAND FOR ANY WAX REMOVAL.<br /> Here are the steps I do to make it easy for me to wax:<br />1: I pre-cut my muslin strips ahead of time and have them ready to use.<br />2: I have baby powder out to apply on the area before I apply the wax.<br />3: Before I even turn the unit on, I put a piece of paper under the heater that is large enough to cover any drips that may happen. I put the collar around the top of the wax can and then put it in the unit and heat it for about a half an hour before I use it. I also put another piece of paper between me and the unit to catch any drips so I don't get any wax on my counter. I also put my used stick there after each use. It makes clean up SO easy- just throw away the paper and you're all done.<br />DO NOT RE-DIP THE STICK AFTER EACH USE. This is for hygiene and keeps your wax clean.<br />4: I make sure to use the pre-wax cleaner first, (so the skin is clean of any oils and bacteria) and then I use a small amount of baby powder over the area to be waxed.<br />5: I put on gloves before I wax. It really makes a difference. I tried to do it without, and somehow always get some wax on me.<br />I stir the wax, dip my stick in and use a small amount and wave it for just a second and apply the wax in the direction of hair growth. For my upper lip, I start in the middle of the lip and apply toward the edge of my lip. Apply the muslin strip and I let it stay there for almost 45 seconds. I have found if I try to remove my strip too soon, the wax doesn't come off. Pull toward the middle of the lip (opposite direction of wax application) Make sure to pull quickly and you can hold the edge of your skin before you pull.<br />Then I do the other side. I use baby oil to remove any left over wax and then put all my sticks, cotton pads, and gloves on the piece of paper and then throw away. VERY EASY<br />I was told that cortisone cream may help after the first time of waxing as it can help reduce the redness.<br />I also save the lid to my wax (put somewhere where nothing can touch it-it's really sticky) so that if I want to change waxes I can.<br />Hope this helps some of you who are new to waxing.<br />Make sure to not spill the wax or you will have trouble cleaning it off of surfaces.<br />I LOVE this kit, and it's not fair to fault the wax, when it's usually the user that is having problems.   512. Like others, I figured why spend money at the salon when I could buy the same thing and do it at home for a fraction of the cost.<br /><br />Facial waxing is not difficult. You just have to be patient, get the wax to the right temperature, a thin layer, let it set for a moment, place the muslin over the wax and take a deep breath when you pull. Do remember that the wax will not get every hair and you will need to invest in a magnifying mirror and a good pair of tweezers.<br /><br />The unit takes about 30 minutes to warm up the wax. On the lowest setting, you will still have a clump of unheated wax in the middle but that is no problem. Just stir and use the outer most liquid. At this temperature, you will not have to blow on the stick to cool it before placing it on your skin.<br /><br />I do not use all the prep lotions that were included since my salon did not and I was comfortable with that. Simple baby oil and a quick washing with your regular mild facial cleanser will take care of any residue that you were not able to blot off with the muslin strip.<br /><br />Even though the wax included is for sensitive skin, I experience itching and a slight discomfort around my eyebrows– but that goes away within a half hour.<br /><br />Though not stated on the box or the description, there are a couple of the collars included so before you add them to your cart, wait until you receive your box and check its contents. I had ordered them not knowing and would have much preferred to order extra muslin or sticks for the same money.<br /><br />I have not had the problem that others have had with the included strips leaving fuzz (not sure if they meant fuzz from the muslin or fuzz as in fine baby hairs) and found them to be very useful with just the right amount of grip.<br /><br />This is a great investment and had paid for itself in just two usages.
